# Investigation: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

**Repository:** grafana/grafana
**Task Type:** Regression Hunt (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After upgrading Grafana from v10.3 to v10.4, some dashboards with table panels fail to render correctly. The table panel's field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import. Users see tables with missing column formatting (column widths, text alignment, cell display modes).

The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON. Dashboards with explicit custom config render correctly.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Which migration function is responsible for the regression
2. The exact conditional logic that fails for dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`
3. Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected
4. Which dashboard schema version triggers the issue
5. The files and functions involved in the migration chain

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on the dashboard migration pipeline, particularly schema version handlers

     8→// migration_utils.go contains shared utility functions used across multiple schema version migrations.
     9→
    10→// GetStringValue safely extracts a string value from a map, returning empty string if not found or not a string
    11→func GetStringValue(m map[string]interface{}, key string) string {
    12→	if value, ok := m[key]; ok {
    13→		if s, ok := value.(string); ok {
    14→			return s
    15→		}
    16→	}
    17→	return ""
    18→}
    19→
    20→// GetBoolValue safely extracts a boolean value from a map, returning false if not found or not a boolean
    21→func GetBoolValue(m map[string]interface{}, key string) bool {
    22→	if value, ok := m[key]; ok {
    23→		if b, ok := value.(bool); ok {
    24→			return b
    25→		}
    26→	}
    27→	return false
    28→}
    29→
    30→// GetIntValue safely extracts an integer value from a map, returning defaultValue if not found or not convertible
    31→func GetIntValue(m map[string]interface{}, key string, defaultValue int) int {
    32→	if value, ok := m[key]; ok {
    33→		if i, ok := ConvertToInt(value); ok {
    34→			return i
    35→		}
    36→	}
    37→	return defaultValue
    38→}
    39→
    40→// GetFloatValue safely extracts a float value from a map, returning defaultValue if not found or not convertible
    41→func GetFloatValue(m map[string]interface{}, key string, defaultValue float64) float64 {
    42→	if value, ok := m[key]; ok {
    43→		if f, ok := ConvertToFloat(value); ok {
    44→			return f
    45→		}
    46→	}
    47→	return defaultValue
    48→}

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V37 normalizes legend configuration to use `showLegend` property consistently.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses inconsistencies in how legend visibility was handled.
     8→// There were two ways to hide the legend:
     9→// 1. Using displayMode: "hidden"
    10→// 2. Using showLegend: false
    11→//
    12→// The migration normalizes both approaches to use showLegend consistently:
    13→// - If displayMode is "hidden" OR showLegend is false, set displayMode to "list" and showLegend to false
    14→// - For all other existing legend objects, ensure showLegend is true
    15→//
    16→// Note: This migration only processes legend configurations that already exist as objects.
    17→// Boolean legend values are not processed by this migration.
    18→//
    19→// Example transformations:
    20→//
    21→// Before migration (hidden displayMode):
    22→//
    23→//	options: {
    24→//	  legend: {
    25→//	    displayMode: "hidden",
    26→//	    placement: "bottom"
    27→//	  }
    28→//	}
    29→//
    30→// After migration:
    31→//
    32→//	options: {
    33→//	  legend: {
    34→//	    displayMode: "list",
    35→//	    showLegend: false,
    36→//	    placement: "bottom"
    37→//	  }
    38→//	}
    39→//
    40→// Before migration (showLegend false):
    41→//
    42→//	options: {
    43→//	  legend: {
    44→//	    displayMode: "table",
    45→//	    showLegend: false
    46→//	  }
    47→//	}

    49→// After migration:
    50→//
    51→//	options: {

    54→//	    showLegend: false

     5→// V39 migrates timeSeriesTable transformation configuration to support extensible per-query options.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original timeSeriesTable transformation design where
     8→// each query could only be configured with a single statistic function. The original refIdToStat
     9→// format was too restrictive for evolving use cases that require multiple configuration parameters
    10→// per query, such as custom formatting, aggregation methods, or display preferences.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating panels with timeSeriesTable transformations (including nested panels in rows)
    14→// 2. Extracting the existing refIdToStat mapping from transformation options
    15→// 3. Converting each refId-statistic pair to the new nested object structure
    16→// 4. Preserving the statistic function while enabling future option expansion
    17→// 5. Skipping transformations that lack valid refIdToStat configuration
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring enables future enhancements while maintaining backward compatibility:
    20→// - Additional per-query options can be added without breaking existing configurations
    21→// - The stat property preserves current functionality exactly as before
    22→// - New features like custom labels, formats, or calculations can be added seamlessly
    23→// - The structure scales better for complex multi-query transformations
    24→//
    25→// Example transformation:
    26→//
    27→// Before migration:
    28→//
    29→//	transformations: [{
    30→//	  id: "timeSeriesTable",
    31→//	  options: {
    32→//	    refIdToStat: {
    33→//	      "A": "mean",
    34→//	      "B": "ma

    34→//	    matcher: { id: "byType", options: "time" },

Now let me create a comprehensive analysis document:

## Grafana Dashboard Migration Pipeline - Comprehensive Analysis

Based on my exploration of the Grafana codebase, here's a detailed understanding of the dashboard migration pipeline:

---

### 1. Main Migration Handler Functions and Their Location

**Primary Files:**
- **Main orchestrator:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go`
- **Schema version handlers:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go`
- **Individual migration implementations:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v*.go` (43 migration versions from v2 to v42)

**Key Entry Point:**
```
Migrate(ctx context.Context, dash map[string]interface{}, targetVersion int) error
```

This function:
- Cleans up dashboard properties (__elements, __inputs, __requires)
- Tracks original transformations and fieldConfig.defaults.custom
- Applies frontend defaults via `applyFrontendDefaults()`
- Applies panel-specific defaults via `applyPanelDefaults()`
- Executes migrations sequentially from current version to target
- Performs cleanup phase to match frontend's `getSaveModel()` behavior

---

### 2. Schema Version Handlers - V38 and Surrounding Versions

**Constants (migrations.go):**
- MIN_VERSION = 0
- LATEST_VERSION = 42

**Version 37 (Legend Normalization):**
- Location: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v37.go`
- Purpose: Normalizes legend configuration to use `showLegend` property consistently
- Converts `displayMode: "hidden"` OR `showLegend: false` → `displayMode: "list"` + `showLegend: false`
- Processes panels recursively, including nested panels in rows
- Only processes legend objects (not boolean values)

93-assistanttext-
## Investigation Complete

I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the dashboard migration v38 table panel regression. Here's a summary of my findings:

### **Root Cause Identified**

The regression occurs due to a **critical timing and ordering issue** in the migration pipeline:

1. **V38 Migration Conditional Logic (v38.go:120-123)** assumes that `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` already exists when processing table panels. If it doesn't exist, the entire table migration is silently skipped.

2. **Panel Defaults Application (frontend_defaults.go:102-117)** creates `fieldConfig.defaults` and `fieldConfig.overrides`, but **does NOT create the `custom` object**.

3. **Original Tracking (frontend_defaults.go:1151-1159)** only sets `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag for panels that had `custom` in the original JSON.

### **Why Explicit `defaults.custom` Dashboards Work**

Dashboards with explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in their saved JSON escape the bug because:
- The tracking flag is set before migrations run
- V38 finds the `custom` object and successfully migrates field overrides
- The cleanup phase preserves the structure based on the flag

### **Key Findings**

- **Affected Version**: Schema v38 (introduced in v10.4)
- **Trigger Condition**: Table panels in dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in the original JSON
- **Silent Failure**: The migration skips the table entirely without error, causing field override configuration to be lost
- **Files Involved**: 
  - `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go` (lines 90-137)
  - `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go` (lines 102-117, 557-662, 1151-1169)
  - `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go` (lines 51-142)

The detailed investig

195\u2192// sortPanelsByGridPos sorts panels by grid position (y first, then x)\n   196\u2192func sortPanelsByGridPos(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n   197\u2192\tpanels := yB\n   233\u2192\t})\n   234\u2192}\n   235\u2192\n   236\u2192// addBuiltInAnnotationQuery adds the built-in \"Annotations & Alerts\" annotation\n   237\u2192func addBuiltInAnnotationQuery(dashboard isEqual(a, b interface{}) bool {\n   666\u2192\tif a == nil && b == nil {\n   667\u2192\t\treturn true\n   668\u2192\t}\n   669\u2192\tif a == nil || b == nil {\n   670\u2192\t\treturn false\n The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it\n// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.\n//\n// The migration works by:\n// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)\n// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties\n// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode\n// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path\n// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features\n//\n// This restructuring provides several key benefits:\n// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)\n// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations\n// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode\n// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality\n//\n// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,\n// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.\n//\n// Example transformations:\n//\n// Before migration (field defaults):\n//\n//\tfieldConfig: {\n//\t  defaults: {\n//\t    custom: {\n//\t map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\"id\":           panel[\"id\"],\n\t\t\t\"title\":        panel[\"title\"],\n\t\t\t\"gridPos\":      panel[\"gridPos\"],\n\t\t\t\"libraryPanel\": libraryPanel,\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Clear the original panel and copy back only essential properties\n\t\tfor key := range panel {\n\t\t\tdelete(panel, key)\n\t\t}\n\t\tfor key, value := range essentialProps {\n\t\t\tif value != nil {\n\t\t\t\tpanel[key] = value\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn // Skip the rest of the cleanup for library panels\n\t}\n\n\t// Row panel specific cleanup (matches frontend behavior)\n\tcleanupRowPanelProperties(panel)\n\n\t// Track which properties were present in the input to preserve them even if they become empty\n\toriginalProperties := make(map[string]bool)\n\tfor key := range panel {\n\t\toriginalProperties[key] = true\n\t}\n\t// Properties that should never be persisted (notPersistedProperties)\n\tnotPersistedProps := map[string]bool{\n\t\t\"events\":                  true,\n\t\t\"isViewing\":               true,\n\t\t\"isEditing\":               true,\n\t\t\"isInView\":                true,\n\t\t\"hasRefreshed\":            true,\n\t\t\"cachedPluginOptions\":     true, // This is the key one causing issues\n\t\t\"plugin\":                  true,\n\t\t\"queryRunner\":             true,\n\t\t\"replaceVariables\":        true,\n\t\t\"configRev\":               true,\n\t\t\"hasSavedPanelEditChange\": true,\n\t\t\"getDisplayTitle\":         true,\n\t\t\"dataSupport\":             true,\n\t\t\"key\":                     true,\n\t\t\"isNew\":                   true,\n\t\t\"refreshWhenInView\":       true,\n\t\t\"scopedVars\":              true, // Frontend removes scopedVars from save model\n\t}\n\n\t// Default values that should be filtered out if they match (defaults)\n\tdefaults := map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\"gridPos\": map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\"x\": float64(0), \"y\": float64(0), \"h\": float64(3), \"w\": float64(6),\n\t\t},\n\t\t\"targets\": []interface{}{\n\t\t\tmap[string]interface{}{\"refId\": \"A\"},\n\t\t},\n\t\t\"cachedPluginOptions\": map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\"transparent\":         false,\n\t\t\"options\":             map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\"links\":               []interface{}{},\n\t\t\"fieldConfig\": map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\"defaults\":  map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\t\"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n\t\t},\n\t\t\"title\": \"\",\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove notPersistedProperties\n\tfor prop := range notPersistedProps {\n\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n\t}\n\n\t// Filter out properties that match defaults\n\tfor prop, defaultValue := range defaults {\n\t\tif panelValue, exists := panel[prop]; exists {\n\t\t\tif isEqual(panelValue, defaultValue) {\n\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove empty transformations array unless nested panel had them originally\n\tif transformations, ok := panel[\"transformations\"].([]interface{}); ok && len(transformations) == 0 {\n\t\tif panel[\"_originallyHadTransformations\"] != true || !isNested {\n\t\t\tdelete(panel, \"transformations\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove null values recursively to match frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior\n\t// Pass panel type information to help with threshold handling\n\tpanelType := \"\"\n\tif t, ok := panel[\"type\"].(string); ok {\n\t\tpanelType = t\n\t}\n\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(panel, panelType)\n\n\t// Filter out properties that match defaults (matches frontend's isEqual logic)\n\tfilterDefaultValues(panel, originalProperties)\n\n\t// Clean up internal markers\n\tdelete(panel, \"_originallyHadTransformations\")\n\tdelete(panel, \"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\")\n}\n\n// filterDefaultValues removes properties that match the default values (matches frontend's isEqual logic)\nfunc filterDefaultValues(panel map[string]interface{}, originalProperties map[string]bool) {\n\t// Get panel type for panel-specific defaults\n\tpanelType := \"\"\n\tif t, ok := panel[\"type\"].(string); ok {\n\t\tpanelType = t\n\t}\n\n\t// PanelModel defaults from frontend\n\tdefaults := map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\"gridPos\": map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\"x\": 0, \"y\": 0, \"h\": 3, \"w\": 6,\n\t\t},\n\t\t\"targets\": []interface{}{\n\t\t\tmap[string]interface{}{\"refId\": \"A\"},\n\t\t},\n\t\t\"cachedPluginOptions\": map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\"transparent\":         false,\n\t\t\"options\":             map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\"links\":               []interface{}{},\n\t\t\"fieldConfig\": map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\"defaults\":  map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\t\"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n\t\t},\n\t\t\"title\": \"\",\n\t}\n\n\t// Add panel-specific defaults\n\tif panelType == \"table\" {\n\t\t// Remove legacy table properties (matches frontend getSaveModel filtering)\n\t\t// Exception: preserve original properties for old table panels with autoMigrateFrom=\"table-old\"\n\t\tlegacyTableProps := []string{\"pageSize\", \"scroll\", \"fontSize\", \"showHeader\", \"sort\"}\n\t\tfor _, prop := range legacyTableProps {\n\t\t\tif _, exists := panel[prop]; exists {\n\t\t\t\tif autoMigrateFrom, hasAutoMigrate := panel[\"autoMigrateFrom\"]; hasAutoMigrate && autoMigrateFrom == \"table-old\" {\n\t\t\t\t\tif !originalProperties[prop] {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove properties that match defaults, but preserve properties that were originally present\n\tfor prop, defaultValue := range defaults {\n\t\tif panelValue, exists := panel[prop]; exists {\n\t\t\tif isEqual(panelValue, defaultValue) {\n\t\t\t\t// Special case: fieldConfig - handle preservation of original custom object first\n\t\t\t\tif prop == \"fieldConfig\" {\n\t\t\t\t\t// Check if we need to preserve the custom object before removing fieldConfig\n\t\t\t\t\tif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n\t\t\t\t\t\t// Ensure fieldConfig structure exists with custom object\n\t\t\t\t\t\tif fieldConfig, ok := panelValue.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\tif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tif _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tdefaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t// Don't remove fieldConfig if we added custom back\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t// Only remove if it wasn't originally present in the input\n\t\t\t\t\tif !originalProperties[prop] {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove empty targets arrays (frontend removes them in cleanup)\n\tremoveIfDefaultValue(panel, \"targets\", []interface{}{})\n\n\t// Handle case where fieldConfig was removed but originally had custom object\n\tif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n\t\tif _, hasFieldConfig := panel[\"fieldConfig\"]; !hasFieldConfig {\n\t\t\t// Recreate fieldConfig with custom object\n\t\t\tpanel[\"fieldConfig\"] = map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\t\"defaults\": map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\t\t\"custom\": map[string]interface{}{},\n\t\t\t\t},\n\t\t\t\t\"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Clean up fieldConfig to match frontend behavior\n\tif fieldConfig, exists := panel[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{}); exists {\n\t\t// Clean up fieldConfig defaults to match frontend behavior\n\t\tif defaults, hasDefaults := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); hasDefaults {\n\t\t\t// Remove properties that frontend considers as defaults and omits\n\t\t\tcleanupFieldConfigDefaults(defaults, panel)\n\n\t\t\t// Preserve custom object if it was originally present, even if empty\n\t\t\tif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n\t\t\t\tif _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n\t\t\t\t\tdefaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// isEqual checks if two values are equal (simplified version)\nfunc isEqual(a, b interface{}) bool {\n\tif a == nil && b == nil {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\tif a == nil || b == nil {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// For simple types, use direct comparison\n\tswitch aVal := a.(type) {\n\tcase bool:\n\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(bool); ok {\n\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n\t\t}\n\tcase string:\n\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(string); ok {\n\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n\t\t}\n\tcase float64:\n\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(float64); ok {\n\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n\t\t}\n\tcase []interface{}:\n\t\tif bVal, ok := b.([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n\t\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor i, v := range aVal {\n\t\t\t\tif !isEqual(v, bVal[i]) {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\tcase map[string]interface{}:\n\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n\t\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor k, v := range aVal {\n\t\t\t\tif !isEqual(v, bVal[k]) {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// cleanupDashboardForSave applies the same cleanup logic as the frontend\nfunc cleanupDashboardForSave(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n\tremoveNonPersistedProperties(dashboard)\n\tremoveNullValues(dashboard)\n\tcleanupTemplating(dashboard)\n\tcleanupPanels(dashboard)\n\tcleanupDashboardDefaults(dashboard)\n}\n\n// removeNonPersistedProperties removes non-persisted dashboard properties\nfunc removeNonPersistedProperties(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n\tnonPersistedProperties := map[string]bool{\n\t\t\"events\":                           true,\n\t\t\"meta\":                             true,\n\t\t\"panels\":                           true, // handled specially below\n\t\t\"templating\":                       true, // handled specially below\n\t\t\"originalTime\":                     true,\n\t\t\"originalTemplating\":               true,\n\t\t\"originalLibraryPanels\":            true,\n\t\t\"panelInEdit\":                      true,\n\t\t\"panelInView\":                      true,\n\t\t\"getVariablesFromState\":            true,\n\t\t\"formatDate\":                       true,\n\t\t\"appEventsSubscription\":            true,\n\t\t\"panelsAffectedByVariableChange\":   true,\n\t\t\"lastRefresh\":                      true,\n\t\t\"timeRangeUpdatedDuringEditOrView\": true,\n\t\t\"originalDashboard\":                true,\n\t}\n\n\tfor k, v := range nonPersistedProperties {\n\t\t// Do not remove \"panels\" and \"templating\" here, as they are handled specially\n\t\tif (k == \"panels\" || k == \"templating\") && v {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tif v {\n\t\t\tdelete(dashboard, k)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove properties that frontend omits in getSaveModel\n\tdelete(dashboard, \"variables\")\n}\n\n// removeNullValues removes null values to match frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior\nfunc removeNullValues(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n\t// This handles gnetId: null and other null properties\n\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"gnetId\", nil)\n}\n\n// cleanupTemplating cleans up templating to match frontend's getTemplatingSaveModel behavior\nfunc cleanupTemplating(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n\tif templating, ok := dashboard[\"templating\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\tremoveNullValuesRecursively(templating)\n\t\tcleanupTemplatingVariables(templating)\n\t}\n}\n\n// cleanupTemplatingVariables applies variable adapter logic\nfunc cleanupTemplatingVariables(templating map[string]interface{}) {\n\tif list, ok := templating[\"list\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\tfor _, variableInterface := range list {\n\t\t\tif variable, ok := variableInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\tcleanupVariable(variable)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// cleanupVariable cleans up individual variable properties\nfunc cleanupVariable(variable map[string]interface{}) {\n\t// Remove null datasource\n\tremoveIfDefaultValue(variable, \"datasource\", nil)\n\n\t// Remove properties that frontend omits in getSaveModel\n\tdelete(variable, \"index\")\n\n\t// Apply variable type-specific logic\n\tif variableType, ok := variable[\"type\"].(string); ok {\n\t\tswitch variableType {\n\t\tcase \"query\":\n\t\t\t// Query variables: keep options: [] if refresh !== never (matches frontend getSaveModel logic)\n\t\t\trefresh := schemaversion.GetIntValue(variable, \"refresh\", 1) // Default to 1 (onDashboardLoad) if not specified\n\t\t\tif refresh != 0 {                                            // 0 = VariableRefreshNever\n\t\t\t\tif _, hasOptions := variable[\"options\"]; !hasOptions {\n\t\t\t\t\tvariable[\"options\"] = []interface{}{}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase \"constant\":\n\t\t\t// Constant variables: remove options completely\n\t\t\tdelete(variable, \"options\")\n\t\tcase \"datasource\":\n\t\t\t// Datasource variables: always set options to empty array\n\t\t\tvariable[\"options\"] = []interface{}{}\n\t\tcase \"custom\":\n\t\t\t// Custom variables: no special handling (just return rest)\n\t\t\t// This is the default behavior - no additional processing needed\n\t\tcase \"textbox\":\n\t\t\t// Textbox variables: handle query vs originalQuery logic\n\t\t\t// For now, just return rest (no special handling needed for basic cases)\n\t\tcase \"adhoc\":\n\t\t\t// Adhoc variables: no special handling\n\t\t\t// This is the default behavior - no additional processing needed\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// cleanupPanels cleans up panels and ensures panels property always exists\nfunc cleanupPanels(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n\tif panels, ok := dashboard[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t// Filter out repeated panels (matches frontend getPanelSaveModels behavior)\n\t\t// Frontend filters: !(panel.repeatPanelId || panel.repeatedByRow)\n\t\tfilteredPanels := []interface{}{}\n\t\tfor _, panelInterface := range panels {\n\t\t\tif panel, ok := panelInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\t// Skip panels with repeatPanelId or repeatedByRow\n\t\t\t\tif _, hasRepeatPanelId := panel[\"repeatPanelId\"]; hasRepeatPanelId {\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tif _, hasRepeatedByRow := panel[\"repeatedByRow\"]; hasRepeatedByRow {\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tfilteredPanels = append(filteredPanels, panel)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tcleanupPanelList(filteredPanels)\n\t\tsortPanelsByGridPosition(filteredPanels)\n\t\tdashboard[\"panels\"] = filteredPanels\n\t} else {\n\t\t// Ensure panels property exists even if empty (matches frontend behavior)\n\t\tdashboard[\"panels\"] = []interface{}{}\n\t}\n}\n\n// cleanupPanelList cleans up all panels including nested ones\nfunc cleanupPanelList(panels []interface{}) {\n\tfor _, panelInterface := range panels {\n\t\tif panel, ok := panelInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\tcleanupPanelForSaveWithContext(panel, false)\n\n\t\t\t// Handle nested panels in row panels\n\t\t\tif nestedPanels, ok := panel[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\tfor _, nestedPanelInterface := range nestedPanels {\n\t\t\t\t\tif nestedPanel, ok := nestedPanelInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tcleanupPanelForSaveWithContext(nestedPanel, true)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// sortPanelsByGridPosition sorts panels by grid position (matches frontend sortPanelsByGridPos behavior)\nfunc sortPanelsByGridPosition(panels []interface{}) {\n\tsort.SliceStable(panels, func(i, j int) bool {\n\t\tpanelA, okA := panels[i].(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tpanelB, okB := panels[j].(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tif !okA || !okB {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Get gridPos or use default values if missing\n\t\tgridPosA, okA := panelA[\"gridPos\"].(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tgridPosB, okB := panelB[\"gridPos\"].(map[string]interface{})\n\n\t\t// Default gridPos values (matches frontend PanelModel defaults)\n\t\tdefaultY := float64(0)\n\t\tdefaultX := float64(0)\n\n\t\tyA := defaultY\n\t\tif okA {\n\t\t\tif y, ok := gridPosA[\"y\"].(float64); ok {\n\t\t\t\tyA = y\n\t\t\t} else if y, ok := gridPosA[\"y\"].(int); ok {\n\t\t\t\tyA = float64(y)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tyB := defaultY\n\t\tif okB {\n\t\t\tif y, ok := gridPosB[\"y\"].(float64); ok {\n\t\t\t\tyB = y\n\t\t\t} else if y, ok := gridPosB[\"y\"].(int); ok {\n\t\t\t\tyB = float64(y)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif yA == yB {\n\t\t\txA := defaultX\n\t\t\tif okA {\n\t\t\t\tif x, ok := gridPosA[\"x\"].(float64); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\txA = x\n\t\t\t\t} else if x, ok := gridPosA[\"x\"].(int); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\txA = float64(x)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\txB := defaultX\n\t\t\tif okB {\n\t\t\t\tif x, ok := gridPosB[\"x\"].(float64); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\txB = x\n\t\t\t\t} else if x, ok := gridPosB[\"x\"].(int); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\txB = float64(x)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn xA < xB\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn yA < yB\n\t})\n}\n\n// cleanupRowPanelProperties removes default row panel properties that frontend filters out\nfunc cleanupRowPanelProperties(panel map[string]interface{}) {\n\tpanelType, ok := panel[\"type\"].(string)\n\tif !ok || panelType != \"row\" {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// Remove repeat if empty string (default value)\n\tremoveIfDefaultValue(panel, \"repeat\", \"\")\n}\n\n// applyPanelAutoMigration applies the same auto-migration logic as the frontend PanelModel constructor\nfunc applyPanelAutoMigration(panel map[string]interface{}) {\n\tpanelType, ok := panel[\"type\"].(string)\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tvar newType string\n\n\t// Graph needs special logic as it can be migrated to multiple panels\n\t// Including graphite which was previously migrated to graph in the schema version 2 migration in DashboardMigrator.ts\n\t// but this was a bug because in there graphite was set to graph, but since those migrations run\n\t// after PanelModel.restoreModel where autoMigrateFrom is set, this caused the graph migration to be skipped.\n\t// And this resulted in a dashboard with invalid panels.\n\tif panelType == \"graph\" || panelType == \"graphite\" {\n\t\t// Check xaxis mode for special cases\n\t\tnewType = getGraphAutoMigration(panel)\n\t} else {\n\t\t// Check autoMigrateAngular mapping\n\t\tautoMigrateAngular := map[string]string{\n\t\t\t\"table-old\":                \"table\",\n\t\t\t\"singlestat\":               \"stat\",\n\t\t\t\"grafana-singlestat-panel\": \"stat\",\n\t\t\t\"grafana-piechart-panel\":   \"piechart\",\n\t\t\t\"grafana-worldmap-panel\":   \"geomap\",\n\t\t\t\"natel-discrete-panel\":     \"state-timeline\",\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif mappedType, exists := autoMigrateAngular[panelType]; exists {\n\t\t\tnewType = mappedType\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Apply auto-migration if a new type was determined\n\tif newType != \"\" {\n\t\tpanel[\"autoMigrateFrom\"] = panelType\n\t\tpanel[\"type\"] = newType\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc getGraphAutoMigration(panel map[string]interface{}) string {\n\tnewType := \"\"\n\tif xaxis, ok := panel[\"xaxis\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\tif mode, ok := xaxis[\"mode\"].(string); ok {\n\t\t\tswitch mode {\n\t\t\tcase \"series\":\n\t\t\t\t// Check legend values for bargauge\n\t\t\t\tif legend, ok := panel[\"legend\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\t\tif values, ok := legend[\"values\"].(bool); ok && values {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tnewType = \"bargauge\"\n\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tnewType = \"barchart\"\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\tnewType = \"barchart\"\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tcase \"histogram\":\n\t\t\t\tnewType = \"histogram\"\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Default graph migration to timeseries\n\tif newType == \"\" {\n\t\tnewType = \"timeseries\"\n\t}\n\n\treturn newType\n}\n\n// removeNullValuesRecursively removes null values from nested objects and arrays\n// This matches the frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior\nfunc removeNullValuesRecursively(data interface{}) {\n\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(data, \"\")\n}\n\n// removeNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext removes null values from nested objects and arrays\n// This matches the frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior in getSaveModelClone()\nfunc removeNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(data interface{}, panelType string) {\n\tswitch v := data.(type) {\n\tcase map[string]interface{}:\n\t\t// Remove null values from map\n\t\tfor key, value := range v {\n\t\t\tif value == nil {\n\t\t\t\t// Frontend removes null values via JSON serialization, so we should too\n\t\t\t\t// No special case needed for threshold steps\n\t\t\t\tdelete(v, key)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// Recursively process nested values\n\t\t\t\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(value, panelType)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\tcase []interface{}:\n\t\t// Process array elements\n\t\tfor _, item := range v {\n\t\t\tif item != nil {\n\t\t\t\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(item, panelType)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// removeIfDefaultValue removes the key from the map if its value equals the defaultValue\nfunc removeIfDefaultValue(data map[string]interface{}, key string, defaultValue interface{}) {\n\tif val, ok := data[key]; ok && isEqual(val, defaultValue) {\n\t\tdelete(data, key)\n\t}\n}\n\n// cleanupDashboardDefaults removes dashboard-level default values that frontend filters out\nfunc cleanupDashboardDefaults(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n\t// Remove style if it's the default \"dark\" value\n\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"style\", \"dark\")\n\n\t// Remove hideControls if it's the default false value\n\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"hideControls\", false)\n\n\t//   "content": "# Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression\n\n## Summary\n\nThe regression is caused by the interaction between **v38's table migration logic** (`processPanelsV38()` in `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:90-137`) and the **cleanup phase's field config default filtering** (`filterDefaultValues()` in `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:557-662`).\n\nWhen dashboards lack explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in their original JSON, the v38 migration creates and populates a `custom` object during migration. However, this object is later removed during cleanup because it matches the default empty object pattern, and no flag (`_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom`) was set to preserve it. The bug occurs specifically for dashboards where the frontend's panel defaults injection creates the `custom` object after v38 runs, causing field overrides to be silently dropped.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Premature Custom Object Creation and Loss\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:120-123`\n\n```go\n// Line 120-123: V38 assumes custom object exists; if not, silently skips processing\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // REGRESSION: Skips table processing if custom is absent\n}\n```\n\n**The Problem:**\nThe v38 migration checks if `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` exists **after** panel defaults have been applied (line 75 in `migrate.go`). However, the order of operations creates a timing issue:\n\n1. **Line 67-71 (migrate.go):** `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom()` runs and records which panels had `custom` in the **original** input\n2. **Line 75 (migrate.go):** `applyFrontendDefaults()` is called\n3. **Line 79-85 (migrate.go):** `applyPanelDefaults()` creates `fieldConfig.defaults` and `fieldConfig.overrides` but **does NOT create `custom`**\n4. **Line 119-127 (migrate.go):** Schema migrations run, including v38\n5. **Line 135 (migrate.go):** `cleanupDashboardForSave()` runs, which includes cleanup logic\n\n**Critical Gap:** When a dashboard doesn't have `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in the original JSON:\n- `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag is NOT set (line 1155-1157 in `frontend_defaults.go`)\n- `applyPanelDefaults()` creates empty `fieldConfig.defaults` but no `custom` object\n- v38 checks for `custom` existence and **skips the table entirely** if missing\n\n### Secondary Issue: Cleanup Removes Migrated Field Overrides\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:606-620`\n\nEven if v38 created field overrides, the cleanup phase would remove them:\n\n```go\n// Line 606-620: Special handling for fieldConfig during cleanup\nif prop == \"fieldConfig\" {\n    // Check if we need to preserve the custom object before removing fieldConfig\n    if panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n        // Only preserves if original input HAD custom\n        // ...\n    }\n    delete(panel, prop)  // Removes fieldConfig if matches defaults\n}\n```\n\nSince dashboards without explicit `custom` don't have the `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag, the entire `fieldConfig` can be removed, along with any field overrides.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**V38 Migration Function (v38.go:75-86):**\n```go\nfunc V38(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\n    dashboard[\"schemaVersion\"] = int(38)\n\n    panels, ok := dashboard[\"panels\"].([]interface{})\n    if !ok {\n        return nil\n    }\n\n    // Process all panels, including nested ones\n    processPanelsV38(panels)\n\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**ProcessPanelsV38 - The Critical Check (v38.go:90-137):**\n```go\nfunc processPanelsV38(panels []interface{}) {\n    for _, panel := range panels {\n        p, ok := panel.(map[string]interface{})\n        if !ok {\n            continue\n        }\n\n        // ... row recursion ...\n\n        // Only process table panels\n        if p[\"type\"] != \"table\" {\n            continue\n        }\n\n        fieldConfig, ok := p[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{})\n        if !ok {\n            continue\n        }\n\n        defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\n        if !ok {\n            continue\n        }\n\n        custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\n        if !ok {\n            continue  // \u2190 REGRESSION HERE: skips table if custom doesn't exist\n        }\n\n        // Migration only happens if custom exists\n        if displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n            // ... migration logic ...\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Original Tracking (frontend_defaults.go:1151-1159):**\n```go\nfunc trackPanelOriginalFieldConfigCustom(panel map[string]interface{}) {\n    // Mark if this panel had fieldConfig.defaults.custom in original input\n    if fieldConfig, ok := panel[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        if defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n            if _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; hasCustom {\n                panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] = true  // Only set if custom existed\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Cleanup Logic (frontend_defaults.go:606-620):**\n```go\nif prop == \"fieldConfig\" {\n    // Check if we need to preserve the custom object before removing fieldConfig\n    if panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n        // Ensure fieldConfig structure exists with custom object\n        if fieldConfig, ok := panelValue.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n            if defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n                if _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n                    defaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n                }\n                // Don't remove fieldConfig if we added custom back\n                continue\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    delete(panel, prop)  // Removes fieldConfig (and any overrides)\n}\n```\n\n**Panel Defaults Application (frontend_defaults.go:102-117):**\n```go\nif _, exists := panel[\"fieldConfig\"]; !exists {\n    panel[\"fieldConfig\"] = map[string]interface{}{\n        \"defaults\":  map[string]interface{}{},  // \u2190 Empty defaults, NO custom\n        \"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n    }\n} else {\n    // Add missing defaults and overrides\n    if fieldConfig, ok := panel[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        if _, hasDefaults := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"]; !hasDefaults {\n            fieldConfig[\"defaults\"] = map[string]interface{}{}  // \u2190 No custom\n        }\n        if _, hasOverrides := fieldConfig[\"overrides\"]; !hasOverrides {\n            fieldConfig[\"overrides\"] = []interface{}{}\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Migration Pipeline Files\n\n1. **`/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`** (Lines 90-137)\n   - `processPanelsV38()`: Assumes `custom` object exists, skips tables if missing\n   - `migrateOverrides()`: Only runs if table processing succeeds\n\n2. **`/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`** (Lines 557-662)\n   - `filterDefaultValues()`: Removes fieldConfig if matches default (lines 606-620)\n   - `trackPanelOriginalFieldConfigCustom()`: Only flags panels with original custom (lines 1151-1169)\n   - `applyPanelDefaults()`: Creates defaults but not custom (lines 102-117)\n\n3. **`/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go`** (Lines 51-142)\n   - `Migrate()`: Controls execution order of tracking, defaults, and cleanup\n\n### Affected Panel Types\n\n- **Table panels** with field overrides that reference `custom.displayMode`\n- **Only dashboards** with schema version < 38 and NO explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n\n### Migration Chain Trigger\n\n- Affects dashboards imported from v10.3 or earlier that are being migrated to v10.4+ (schema v38+)\n- Specifically those with table panels that have field overrides but no explicit `custom` config in the original JSON\n\n## Why Dashboards with Explicit `defaults.custom` Are Unaffected\n\nDashboards that explicitly include `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in their saved JSON work correctly because:\n\n1. **Original tracking succeeds** (line 1155-1157): `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom = true` is set\n2. **V38 migration executes** (line 120): `custom` object exists, so type assertion succeeds\n3. **Field overrides are migrated** (line 135-179): `custom.displayMode` \u2192 `custom.cellOptions`\n4. **Cleanup preserves the structure** (line 655-659): Because the flag is set, `fieldConfig` is not removed\n\nThe protection is only in place for panels that **originally had** the `custom` object in the JSON.\n\n## Affected Dashboard Schema Version\n\n- **Triggers on:** Dashboard schema version < 38 (v10.3 and earlier)\n- **Fixed by:** Schema version 38 migration (intended fix)\n- **Bug manifests:** When v38 migration runs on dashboards lacking original `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n\n## Specific Conditional Logic Failure\n\n**The exact failing condition (v38.go:120-123):**\n\n```go\n// This condition fails when:\n// 1. Panel is a table\n// 2. fieldConfig.defaults exists (created by applyPanelDefaults)\n// 3. fieldConfig.defaults.custom does NOT exist (not in original JSON, not created by defaults)\n\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // Silent skip - no migration happens, no error is raised\n}\n```\n\n**Why it's a regression:**\n- The frontend's DashboardModel and PanelModel constructors **do create** default structures during UI rendering\n- The migration assumes these structures already exist before v38 runs\n- But `applyPanelDefaults()` doesn't create the `custom` object, only `defaults` and `overrides`\n- This creates a **mismatch between what the migration expects and what frontend defaults provide**\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires one of these strategies:\n\n1. **Option A (Preferred - Matches Frontend Behavior):** Modify `applyPanelDefaults()` to create `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` as an empty object for all panels, matching what the frontend PanelModel constructor does. This ensures v38 always has the `custom` object to work with.\n\n2. **Option B (Backward-Compatible):** Modify v38's `processPanelsV38()` to create the `custom` object if it doesn't exist before processing:\n   ```go\n   if _, ok := defaults[\"custom\"]; !ok {\n       defaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n   }\n   // Then proceed with migration\n   ```\n\n3. **Option C (Tracking-Based):** Modify the tracking logic to mark all tables as needing migration, not just those with explicit `custom`, and handle the object creation during v38 cleanup phase.\n\n**Key Insight:** The root cause is the gap between when the tracking (`trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom`) occurs and when the panel defaults (`applyPanelDefaults`) are applied. The `custom` object is neither tracked nor created before v38 runs, causing the migration to silently skip tables that should be migrated.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

## Summary

The regression is caused by the interaction between **v38's table migration logic** (`processPanelsV38()` in `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:90-137`) and the **cleanup phase's field config default filtering** (`filterDefaultValues()` in `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:557-662`).

When dashboards lack explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in their original JSON, the v38 migration creates and populates a `custom` object during migration. However, this object is later removed during cleanup because it matches the default empty object pattern, and no flag (`_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom`) was set to preserve it. The bug occurs specifically for dashboards where the frontend's panel defaults injection creates the `custom` object after v38 runs, causing field overrides to be silently dropped.

## Root Cause

### Primary Issue: Premature Custom Object Creation and Loss

**Location:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:120-123`

```go
// Line 120-123: V38 assumes custom object exists; if not, silently skips processing
custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue  // REGRESSION: Skips table processing if custom is absent
}
```

**The Problem:**
The v38 migration checks if `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` exists **after** panel defaults have been applied (line 75 in `migrate.go`). However, the order of operations creates a timing issue:

1. **Line 67-71 (migrate.go):** `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom()` runs and records which panels had `custom` in the **original** input
2. **Line 75 (migrate.go):** `applyFrontendDefaults()` is called
3. **Line 79-85 (migrate.go):** `applyPanelD
... (truncated)
